            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Taylor owns an interesting bat -- one that possesses power that blends well with his natural speed. Of now, though, he’s not good enough at making contact to take advantage of his raw skills. Outside of last year’s .313 batting average in Double-A, Taylor’s never hit above .263 at any level over an extended period of time. He will take a walk -- that helps, but it isn’t enough until he begins marking more contact. And since the Nationals are pretty well set in the outfield, you get a cloudy playing time situation. Unless Taylor is traded or is filling in for an injured player, he isn’t likely to see a good number of plate appearances. With Jayson Werth's surgery, there's a chance he's valuable to begin the season, but will that opportunity be enough to count on him for the full season?  (Landon Jones)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Taylor is an interesting name to watch, because of his power/speed potential, but there are simply too many questions marks to think about him too deeply right now. If he shows growth at the dish, though, things could change in a hurry.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>There’s plenty for fantasy owners to be excited about with Taylor. He was one of 16 players to collect 14 home runs and 16 steals last season. He’ll be 25 years old on Opening Day. If things break right, there’s room for him at the top of a solid lineup meaning he could be asset in runs despite a career .282 on-base percentage. Unfortunately, that optimism is held in check because he has struggled to make steady contact and no longer has a starting job. His swinging strike rate was among the worst in baseball last season and he didn’t carry the kind of power upside found among many of the names with similar flaws. Those contact problems seem to have spooked the Nationals, who traded for Ben Revere to play center field. While not usually relevant for fantasy, Taylor’s excellent defense is important here because it’s an asset in his fight for playing time. Unless there’s an injury, Taylor will be limited to possibly platooning with Revere against some lefties and filling in on the occasional day off for 36-year-old left fielder Jayson Werth. Despite the contact and playing time troubles, Taylor is worth a look late in deep fantasy drafts since he is young enough to improve and has proven power / speed production. (Adam McFadden)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Taylor’s age and production last season mean he has the all-important upside, without a hefty draft cost. He certainly has room to become a fantasy star if he can find enough playing time and make more consistent contact.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Two years ago,Taylor looked like the Nationals' center fielder of the future. He was a rangy outfielder with a tantalizing power-speed combo who also drew walks. He feasted on Double-A pitching in 2014, but did so with an unsightly strikeout rate. Unfortunately, his propensity to swing-and-miss has prevented him from having any sort of success over his first 800 plate appearances in the big leagues.Taylor's power and speed have both carried over to the show, but that hasn't much mattered, as his putrid .281 OBP has kept him out of the lineup. With Adam Eaton now in the fold, Taylor will seemingly enter the year as the Nationals' fourth outfielder. Though it shouldn't be terribly hard for him to steal at-bats from Jayson Werth; and Bryce Harper hasn't exactly been a bastion of health in his young career. If he somehow finds regular playing time,Taylor could easily put up a 20-20 season, albeit with a sub-.240 average. It just isn't clear he'll get that chance in 2017. <a href="https://twitter.com/_chris_mitchell">(Chris Mitchell)</a><br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Taylor's power and speed make him an intriguing option in fantasy, but his inability to get on base keeps him out of the lineup. It's probably best to look elsewhere unless he somehow secures a regular gig.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
